## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv/dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t through restoring forces, nonlinear stiffness, damping, and/or external driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (Duffing with damping and periodic drive)
- Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping depending on amplitude)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (polynomial potential)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coupled position-velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v (mixed nonlinear coupling)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (quadratic restoring with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, xآ³, xâپµ) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium â€” expect symmetric potentials to use only odd powers of x
- Even-power terms in x (xآ²) break oscillation symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent energy dissipation (damping) or injection; sign determines which
- Terms like xآ²آ·v indicate amplitude-dependent damping (self-excitation or self-limiting behavior as in Van der Pol)
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(cآ·t) or cos(cآ·t) indicates external periodic forcing â€” look for resonance phenomena
- If t does not appear explicitly, the system is autonomous and conservation/dissipation arguments apply
- Cubic terms in x with opposite sign to linear term indicate Duffing-type hardening (same sign) or softening (opposite sign) spring
- Products of v with powers of x suggest nonlinear friction or state-dependent damping mechanisms

Let me check each candidate systematically:

**Candidates 1-4:** These contain terms like `v`, `vآ³`, `v*x` but no `sin(x)` or `sin(v)`. Since `sin(v)` cannot be represented by polynomials in v (linear independence of polynomial and trigonometric basis functions), these cannot match. Similarly, `v*sin(x)` cannot be represented by `v*x`.

**Candidates 5-6, 9-22, 29, 32-34:** Same issue - they lack `sin(v)` and `v*sin(x)` terms. They use polynomial/rational/log functions of x and v instead.

**Candidates 7-8:** These have `sin(c3*x + c4)` and `v*x` terms. `sin(c3*x+c4)` could provide `sin(x)`, but `v*x â‰  v*sin(x)` and there's no `sin(v)` term. No match.

**Candidates 23-28, 30-31:** These have `v/(c+x)âپ´` type terms. This rational function cannot equal `v*sin(x) + sin(v)`. No match.

**Candidates 35-50:** These are complex rational expressions with denominators `(c1+v)`. Let me check if any can produce `sin(v)` and `v*sin(x)` terms. All of these candidates have terms like `xآ³/(c1+v)`, `v*xآ³/(c1+v)`, `sin(t)/(c1+v)`, `v*sin(t)/(c1+v)`, `v/(c1+v)`. None contain `sin(x)` or `sin(v)` as basis functions. The transcendental functions `sin(x)` and `sin(v)` are completely absent from all these candidates.

Let me double-check: Could any combination of the terms in any candidate reproduce both `v*sin(x)` and `sin(v)`?

- `v*sin(x)`: This requires a `sin(x)` basis function multiplied by `v`. No candidate (except 7, 8, 27, 31 which have `sin(c*x+c)`) has this, and even those don't have it multiplied by `v`.
- `sin(v)`: This requires a sinusoidal function of `v`. NO candidate has `sin(v)` anywhere.

Since `sin(v)` is a required term in the GT and cannot be represented by any polynomial, rational, exponential, or other non-sinusoidal function of `v`, and no candidate contains `sin(v)`, none can match.

Similarly, `v*sin(x)` requires both `v` and `sin(x)` multiplied together, which no candidate provides.
